The Teleological Argument: Purpose in the Universe
Buti presents the teleological proof for God's existence from order and purpose in creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the teleological argument (proof of wisdom and harmony) as presented by Buti, and how it uses the directedness of the universe to prove the existence of a Creator.

Core Idea
The universe's purpose and harmony point to a Planner, just as human devices do.

In this passage, Buti guides us to reflect on the purpose evident in ourselves and in all of creation. He builds a powerful analogy: if human-made tools require a designer because they cannot direct themselves toward a goal, then the vast cosmic 'device'—the universe—must also have a Planner. This is a classic teleological argument, rooted in Quranic teaching.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how Buti moves from your own self to the whole universe.
Buti uses a contemplative style—try to follow his reasoning step by step.
2
Identify the key analogy
Find where Buti compares human artifacts to the universe. What does he say about each?
The analogy is the heart of the argument.
3
Understand the conclusion
After the analogy, Buti states that the universe's design proves a Creator (مدبر). How does he support this?
He calls this the 'proof of wisdom and harmony'.
4
Reflect on Quranic support
Buti notes that the Quran repeatedly uses this argument. Think of examples from the Quran that point to purpose in creation.
This shows the argument's centrality in Islam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتتأمل في ذاتك وما أودع فيها من القوى المدركة (وأنت جزء من الكون كما تعلم) فتجد أنك قد أعطيت سلاحاً لا ينتهي العجب من شأنه ولا يقف عقل العالمين كلهم على حقيقته. وتتأمل فتعلم أن لوجود هذه القوة غاية معينة: أن تسخر بها كل ما تراه حولك من مظاهر المكونات، وأن تمتلك بها مقاليد الاستفادة منها، وأن تسبر غورها وتصل إلى جذورها وقوى الفاعلية فيها. وقس على هذا الذي ذكرته لك سائر مظاهر الكون المختلفة التي تراها أو يصل فكرك إليها. فسترى أنها جميعاً تسير نحو غايات معينة تمد هذا الوجود بالتناسق والتنظيم، وتمد الإنسان بالرحمة والقدرة على كل ما هو بسبيله من شؤونه المختلفة. إذا علمت هذا، فلا مناص من أن تستيقن ما يلي: كما أننا نقول أن ظهور العلة الغائية في الأجهزة والمصنوعات الإنسانية المختلفة دليل قطعي على وجود مدبر صممها على هذا النحو، إذ لا تملك الأجهزة الجامدة أن تفكر لتسير بنفسها نحو غايات معينة - فإن ظهور العلة الغائية في هذا الجهاز الأعظم، الذي هو الكون، بهذا المظهر العجيب، دليل قطعي أيضاً على أن من ورائه مدبراً له يدفعه في طريق غاياته هذه، وهي غايات لا يمكن أن تلتقي أجهزة البشر كلها (متعاونة) على استهداف مثلها. هذه الحقيقة الواضحة، التي تشكل برهاناً يقينياً آخر على وجود الله جل جلاله، والتي يسميها الغربيون (العلة الغائية) وعلماء الكلام (دليل الحكمة والتناسق)، هي التي يظل القرآن يوجه العقول إليها بأساليب رائعة مختلفة يفهمها الناس على اختلاف مستوياتهم وثقافاتهم. وهو برهان يخرس ألسنة الملحدين ويسد دونهم منافذ الحيل كلها.
And you contemplate yourself and what has been deposited in you of perceptive faculties (and you are a part of the universe, as you know), and you find that you have been given a weapon whose wonder is endless and the minds of all the worlds cannot grasp its reality. And you contemplate and learn that the existence of this power has a specific purpose: that you subdue by it all that you see around you of manifestations of components, and that you possess by it the reins of benefiting from them, and that you probe its depth and reach its roots and the active forces within them. And analogize to this that I have mentioned to you all the various manifestations of the universe that you see or your thought reaches. You will see that they all proceed towards specific purposes that supply this existence with harmony and organization, and supply man with mercy and ability in all his various affairs that he undertakes. If you know this, there is no escape from being certain of the following: Just as we say that the appearance of the final cause in various human devices and artifacts is a definitive proof of the existence of a planner who designed them in this way, since inanimate devices cannot think to proceed by themselves towards specific purposes—so the appearance of the final cause in this greatest device, which is the universe, in this wondrous manner, is also a definitive proof that behind it there is a planner who drives it on the path of these purposes, purposes that all human devices (cooperating) cannot aim to achieve. This clear truth, which constitutes another certain proof of the existence of Allah, Exalted is His Majesty, and which Westerners call (the final cause) and theologians (the proof of wisdom and harmony), is what the Quran continually directs minds towards with various wonderful methods that people understand according to their different levels and cultures. And it is a proof that silences the tongues of atheists and closes off all avenues of ruse against them.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage presents the teleological argument (العلة الغائية) for God's existence. Buti begins by inviting the reader to contemplate the human self and its faculties, noting that even this small part of the universe shows purpose. He then generalizes: all manifestations of the universe are directed toward specific goals, providing harmony and organization. The key analogy is that human-made devices (e.g., tools, machines) clearly require a designer because they cannot move themselves toward a purpose; similarly, the universe as a whole is a vast device exhibiting intricate design and purpose, so it must have a Creator (مدبر). Buti identifies this argument as the 'proof of wisdom and harmony' (دليل الحكمة والتناسق) and emphasizes that the Quran repeatedly calls attention to it. He concludes that this proof shuts down all atheistic objections.

Key Terms
العلة الغائية
دليل الحكمة والتناسق
مدبر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The design argument only points to complexity or order, not purpose.
Correction: Buti emphasizes that the key is 'غاية' (purpose/directedness), not just complexity. The universe is goal-oriented, which requires a Planner.

Checkpoint
What is the central analogy Buti uses to support the teleological argument?
A) A watch and a watchmaker
B) Human devices and artifacts requiring a planner vs. the universe requiring a Creator
C) A poem formed by chance vs. a designed poem
D) The human soul as proof of God

Key Takeaway
The teleological argument uses the directedness and purpose in the universe to prove a Creator, just as human devices show a designer.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage invites you to contemplate the purpose in your own self. When was the last time you genuinely paused to reflect on the intricate faculties Allah has placed in you? What would it take for you to make such reflection a daily habit, rather than rushing past this proof?
?
Buti claims this argument silences atheists and closes off all avenues of ruse. Yet, do you live as if this truth is certain? In moments of doubt or when faced with life's hardships, does your heart anchor itself in the certainty that everything has a purpose from Allah? What one change can you make today to strengthen that certainty in your daily life?
?
The Quran repeatedly directs minds to this proof, but many Muslims read it without true contemplation. Are you among those who recite the signs without letting them pierce your heart? What would it mean for you to truly believe that your existence has a purpose set by the Creator? How would that change your decisions today?

Refutation of the Chance Objection Using the Letters Analogy
Buti refutes the chance hypothesis with Mustafa Sabri's argument against random assembly.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the chance objection to the design argument fails, and how Mustafa Sabri's critique exposes its hidden assumption of design.

Core Idea
Chance cannot produce order; the objection secretly assumes the design it denies.

In this passage, Buti confronts a common skeptical objection: perhaps the universe's order is just a product of random chance over vast time. He presents an atheist's analogy of scattering letters to form a poem, then demolishes it using Mustafa Sabri's razor-sharp rebuttal. Sabri shows that the objection either requires preserving partial order (which is design) or leads to endless destruction, making completion impossible.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Notice the flow: Buti sets up the objection, then responds with Sabri's argument.
Pay attention to the atheist's scenario and Sabri's logical steps.
2
Identify the hidden assumption
Sabri argues that for the analogy to work, the atheist must assume that parts of the poem that form are preserved in subsequent scatterings. Without that assumption, progress is impossible.
Why is preservation an act of design? It requires intention to keep what formed.
3
Understand the refutation's core
Disorder does not spontaneously become order, even over infinite time. Time only increases chaos. The atheist's scenario either fails or contradicts its own premise.
This refutation applies to any chance-based explanation of cosmic order.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غير أن من أراد الله عز وجل أن يحيق به عقابه الخالد إذ لم يشكر نعمة العقل الذي في رأسه فيستعمله في البحث الحر يجعل عقله في غطاء القطعية كلها. ولذلك لا تعجب أن تجد قائلاً منهم يقول من هذه البراهين البدهية: إن كل ما تقوله يحتمل أن يكون بمحض المصادفة... ويذهب يمثل كيف أن ذلك يحتمل، فيقول: إننا لو نثرنا كمية كبيرة من الحروف المطبعية على سطح فسيح أملاً في أن يتشكل منها ديوان شعر لمثل (هوميروس) أو (فيكتور هوجو) وتكررت هذه المحاولة سنوات طويلة تقدر بالملايين، فربما يحصل في كل مرة أو مرات من نثر تلك الحروف تشكل جزء من تلك القصائد ثم جزء آخر، وهكذا حتى يكتمل الديوان خلال الزمن الطويل ذاك!.. فأنت إذا تأملت في هذا الكلام، وجدت الرجل يهذي بما لا يعقل! بل إنك لتعجب من أن يصل به الهذيان - وهو يصطنع البحث والفكر - إلى هذا الحد. ولأنقل لك في تصوير هذا الهذيان ما يقوله تعقيباً عليه العلامة الأستاذ مصطفى صبري في كتابه موقف العقل: يُردُّ عليه بأن عدم الانتظام لا يتحول بنفسه إلى نظام ولو دام ألف ألف عام، بل يزيده الدوام تشوشاً وارتباكاً، ولا يجديهم نفعاً تصور احتمال تشكل جزء من قصائد الديوان في كل فترة، إذ لا يكون من حقهم أن يفرضوا حفظ الجزء المتشكل ونثر ما عداه في المرة الثانية حتى يتشكل جزء آخر، وهكذا إلى أن يتم شكل القصائد كلها - بل يلزم أن يفرض في كل مرة نثر جميع الحروف المنثورة في المرة الأولى الشاملة لحروف الجزء المتشكل، فينقض في المرة الثانية ما انتظم في الأولى، وإن كان في الإمكان تشكل جزء فسينتقض هو الآخر في المرة الثانية، ولو لم نفرض هكذا، لكان حفظ الأجزاء المتشكلة في أي مرة وحصر تكرار النثر في الباقي بعد تلك الأجزاء - نظاماً مقصوداً، فيلزم خلاف المفروض الذي هو عدم القصد إلى النظام. (1) موقف العقل: 2 / 348.
But whoever Allah, Mighty and Majestic, wills to visit with His eternal punishment—since he did not thank for the blessing of the mind in his head, using it in free inquiry—makes his mind in a covering of absolute denial. Therefore do not be surprised to find a speaker among them saying of these self-evident proofs: 'Everything you say could be by pure chance...' And he goes on to illustrate how that is possible, saying: 'If we scattered a large quantity of typographical letters on a wide surface hoping that a collection of poetry like Homer's or Victor Hugo's would form from them, and this attempt was repeated for millions of years, perhaps in each time or times of scattering those letters, a part of those poems would form, then another part, and so on until the collection is completed over that long time!' So if you contemplate this speech, you find the man raving irrationally! Indeed, you are amazed that his raving—while he affects research and thought—reaches this extent. And to convey to you this raving, I quote what the esteemed scholar Mustafa Sabri says in his book 'Mawqif al-'Aql' in response: 'It is refuted by the fact that disorder does not turn by itself into order even if it lasts a thousand thousand years, rather duration increases it in confusion and disarray. Nor does the imagined possibility of a part of the poems forming in each period benefit them, because they have no right to assume the preservation of the part that formed and the scattering of the rest in the second time until another part forms, and so on until all the poems are formed. Rather, they must assume that in each time all the letters scattered in the first time, including the letters of the part that formed, are scattered, so what was ordered in the first time is undone in the second. And if it were possible for another part to form, it too would be undone in the second time. And if we do not assume this, then preserving the parts that formed in any time and restricting the repetition of scattering to the remainder after those parts would be an intended order, which contradicts the assumption, which is the absence of intention towards order.' (1) Mawqif al-'Aql: 2/348.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage presents and refutes the chance objection to the design argument. An atheist claims the universe's order could result from random processes, analogous to scattering letters randomly to eventually form a poem. Buti quotes Mustafa Sabri's rebuttal: disorder does not spontaneously become order over time; rather, time increases chaos. Crucially, the atheist's scenario implicitly assumes that once a part of the poem forms, it is preserved for subsequent scatterings (otherwise it would be destroyed), which is itself an instance of design. Without preservation, each new scattering destroys previous 'progress', making completion impossible. Thus, the objection self-destructs because it covertly assumes the very intentional order it denies.

Key Terms
المصادفة
النظام
عدم الانتظام
القصد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that given enough time, random processes can produce complex order like the universe or a poem.
Correction: Sabri shows that time does not convert disorder into order; it increases chaos. Additionally, any 'progress' requires preservation, which is itself a form of design.

Checkpoint
What is the key flaw Mustafa Sabri identifies in the chance (letters) objection?
A) Random scattering can never produce any order even over infinite time
B) The objector must assume preservation of existing order to allow progress, which contradicts the assumption of no design
C) The number of letters is too large for chance to work
D) The universe is more complex than a poem

Key Takeaway
The chance objection fails because it cannot account for the preservation of partial order without assuming the very design it denies.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you receive a good outcome—like success in work or safety from harm—do you ever attribute it to 'luck' or 'chance' rather than to Allah? What would change in your heart if you replaced every 'luck' with 'the order of Allah's decree'?
?
This lesson shows that preservation of partial order requires intention. In your own life, what 'partial orders'—habits, relationships, or faith—are you passively letting time erode? Are you intentionally preserving what matters for your akhirah, or leaving it to chance?
?
Imagine you truly believed that every pattern you see—from the cosmos to your own heartbeat—is pure chance. How would that affect your gratitude, your responsibility, and your hope? Can you live consistently with that belief, or does the evidence of design compel you to submit?

Refuting the Chance Argument for Order
Buti presents and refutes the atheist chance argument using Mustafa Sabri's reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the 'chance over time' argument for the origin of order is logically flawed and requires hidden intentionality.

Core Idea
Disorder cannot spontaneously become order, even with infinite time.

The atheist's chance argument attempts to explain the order in the universe by appealing to random events over vast time. Buti presents this argument and then refutes it using Mustafa Sabri's analysis. The refutation reveals that the argument secretly assumes an ordering principle.

Guided Path
1
Read the atheist's analogy
Read the passage describing the scattering of letters to form a poetry collection. Notice how it mirrors the 'infinite monkeys' argument.
The analogy is meant to show that order could arise by chance given enough time.
2
Understand Buti's immediate criticism
Buti dismisses the argument as irrational raving. Reflect on why he finds it so obviously flawed.
He sets up the stronger refutation that follows.
3
Analyze Mustafa Sabri's logical refutation
Work through Sabri's key point: to avoid undoing previous progress, the chance process must preserve parts already formed—but that preservation is itself an intentional system, contradicting the assumption of pure chance.
This exposes the hidden assumption in the chance argument.

Therefore do not be surprised to find one of them saying: 'Everything you say could be by mere chance...' and he goes on to illustrate how that is possible, saying: 'If we scattered a large quantity of printing letters on a spacious surface hoping that a collection of poetry like Homer or Victor Hugo would form from them, and this attempt was repeated for millions of years, then perhaps in each time or times of scattering those letters a part of those poems would form, then another part, and so on until the collection was completed over that long time!' Then when you reflect on this speech, you find the man raving irrationally! Indeed you are amazed that raving reaches this extent while he pretends to be engaged in research and thought. And to depict this raving for you, I will present what the scholar al-Ustadh Mustafa Sabri says in response to it in his book 'Mawqif al-Aql': It is refuted by the fact that disorder does not transform by itself into order even if it lasted a thousand thousand years; rather duration increases it in confusion and disorder. And the conception of the possibility of a part of the poems of the collection forming in each period does not benefit them, because it is not within their right to assume preservation of the formed part and scattering of what remains in the second time until another part forms, and so on until all poems are fully formed. Rather, it is necessary to assume that in each time all the letters scattered in the first time—including the letters of the formed part—are scattered, so that what was ordered in the first time is undone in the second time. And if it were possible for another part to form, it too would be undone in the second time. And if we do not assume this, then preserving the parts formed at any time and limiting the repetition of scattering to what remains after those parts would be an intended order, so it would contradict the assumption which is the absence of intention for order.

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer unit. First, the atheist's objection is presented: he gives an analogy involving scattering letters randomly to eventually form a complete collection of poetry by chance over immense time. The author immediately labels this as irrational raving. Then the real answer comes via a quotation from Mustafa Sabri. The refutation makes a key point: disorder cannot become order on its own; time only increases confusion. The chance scenario fails because to make it work, one would have to assume that the partially formed parts are preserved and only the remaining letters are scattered again—but that itself is an intentional system, not random. If we instead assume that all letters are re-scattered each time, any partial order is undone. Thus the assumption of pure chance without intention is self-contradictory.

Denial of Teleology Becomes Proof of God
Buti shows atheists denying purpose in organs, then turns their irrationality into a divine proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Buti transforms the atheist's denial of purpose in creation into a compelling proof for God's existence.

Core Idea
The atheist's irrational refusal to see purpose is itself a divine sign.

Buti continues his engagement with atheist arguments, this time addressing an even more extreme denial: that bodily organs have no intended functions. The atheist claims that eyes, ears, and the brain just happened to align with their uses by chance, purely to avoid admitting a purposeful Creator. Buti then turns this very irrationality into a powerful argument for God's existence, showing how the atheist's own mental block is evidence of divine control.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the structure: first Buti describes the atheist's claim, then he gives his rebuttal.
Pay attention to the key terms like علل غائية and مصادفة.
2
Identify the atheist's reasoning
Understand why the atheist denies teleology: to avoid having to admit a Creator. See how they replace purpose with chance.
The atheist's motive is to escape the logical implication of a Maker.
3
Analyze Buti's counter-argument
Buti says the atheist's inability to see the obvious is itself proof of God. Why? Because the intellect is not mechanical; its suspension shows it is under divine will.
The argument hinges on the idea that clear signs are deliberately hidden from the arrogant.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وليس هذا هو مبلغ هذيانهم العجيب ، بل إنهم ليشتطون عن ذلك إلى إنكار أن تكون العيون مخلوقة فينا للإبصار ، والآذان للسمع ، والعقل للتفكر والفهم إذ لو لم ينكروا ذلك للزم عليهم القول بأنها مخلوقة لعلل غائية ، وتكون حينئذ مصنوعة لهذه الفائدة من قبل صانع فعل ذلك عن إرادة . فيتهربون عن هذا اللزوم ، ولو كلفهم ذلك أن ينهضوا بأعباء مكابرة لا يتصورها العقل . فتراهم يقولون : إن العين التقت مع الإبصار بمحض المصادفة ، والتقت الأذن بالسمع بمحض المصادفة أيضاً ، والتقى هذا المخ [الناطقة؟] في جوف الرأس مع الفكر بمحض المصادفة أيضاً وأنا أقول : لعمري ولعمر الحق ، إن هذا الهذيان نفسه من أبلغ البراهين بوجود الله !.. فما كان للعقل أن يتعطل عن الاهتداء إلى أوضح ما هو واضح أمامه ، لو أن سيره إلى فهم الأشياء كان بشكل آلي مجرد . أما وقد تعطل عن الفهم رغم وجوده ووجود كل مقومات الفهم ) بعد أن جنح صاحبه إلى الإلحاد في ذات الله واستكبر عن التأمل المنصف ( فإنه لأبلغ دليل على أن هذه القوة إنما هي من تدبير فاطر حكيم أوقفها عن الإنتاج في رأس هذا المستكبر ، جزاء لاستكباره ، وتحقيقاً لسبب عقابه الخالد يوم القيامة .
And this is not the extent of their wondrous raving; rather they go beyond that to denying that eyes are created in us for sight, ears for hearing, and the intellect for reflection and understanding. For if they did not deny that, they would be compelled to say that they are created for teleological purposes, and then they would be made for this benefit by a Maker who did so by will. So they flee from this necessitation, even if it costs them to bear the burdens of stubbornness that reason cannot conceive. And I say: By my life and by the life of truth, this very raving is among the most conclusive proofs of the existence of God! For the intellect would not have been disabled from finding guidance to what is most obviously clear before it, if its course in understanding things had been purely mechanical. But since it has been disabled from understanding despite its existence and the existence of all the elements of understanding, after its possessor deviated into atheism regarding the essence of God and considered himself too great for fair reflection, then it is the most conclusive evidence that this power is only under the management of a wise Creator who stopped its production in the head of this arrogant one, as a recompense for his arrogance, and to realize the cause of his eternal punishment on the Day of Judgment.

Commentary

If the intellect were purely mechanical, it would always see the obvious; but here, due to arrogance and atheism, the intellect shuts down. This shows that the intellect is under divine control—God can 'turn it off' as punishment. Thus their stubbornness itself is evidence of a wise Creator who holds back understanding from the arrogant.

From Denial to Divine Proof
Al-Buti transforms the materialist denial into a proof for God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the denial of purpose in creation by materialists actually serves as a proof for the existence of God, and why atheism is fundamentally opposed to reason.

Core Idea
Atheism's irrational denial of purpose reveals divine intervention.

Al-Buti presents a striking reversal of the materialist argument: the very fact that atheists deny the obvious purpose of our organs—and do so against reason—itself becomes a powerful proof for God. In this passage, he exposes the absurd lengths materialists go to avoid acknowledging a Creator, then turns their irrationality into evidence of divine control.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to absorb the author's tone and argument. Then read the translation to ensure you grasp the full meaning.
Notice the parenthetical remarks—they contain the core argument.
2
Identify the materialist position and its motive
The author describes materialists denying that eyes, ears, and mind are created for their functions. Ask: why do they deny this? What are they trying to avoid?
They deny purpose to avoid concluding there is a purposeful Creator.
3
Understand the author's counter-argument
The author says this very irrationality is a proof of God. If the mind worked mechanically, it would see the obvious purpose; its failure to do so shows divine withholding of understanding as punishment for arrogance.
This is the key reversal: the denial itself becomes evidence.

Source Text

وليس هذا هو مبلغ هذيانهم العجيب ، بل إنهم ليشتطون عن ذلك إلى إنكار أن تكون العيون مخلوقة فينا للإبصار ، والآذان للسمع ، والعقل للتفكر والفهم إذ لو لم ينكروا ذلك للزم عليهم القول بأنها مخلوقة لعلل غائية ، وتكون حينئذ مصنوعة لهذه الفائدة من قبل صانع فعل ذلك عن إرادة . فيتهربون عن هذا اللزوم ، ولو كلفهم ذلك أن ينهضوا بأعباء مكابرة لا يتصورها العقل . فتراهم يقولون : إن العين التقت مع الإبصار بمحض المصادفة ، والتقت الأذن بالسمع بمحض المصادفة أيضاً ، والتقى هذا المخ في جوف الرأس مع الفكر بمحض المصادفة الناطقة (أيضاً وأنا أقول : لعمري ولعمر الحق ، إن هذا الهذيان نفسه من أبلغ البراهين بوجود الله !.. فما كان للعقل أن يتعطل عن الاهتداء إلى أوضح ما هو واضح أمامه ، لو أن سيره إلى فهم الأشياء كان بشكل آلي مجرد . أما وقد تعطل عن الفهم رغم وجوده ووجود كل مقومات الفهم ) بعد أن جنح صاحبه إلى الإلحاد في ذات الله واستكبر عن التأمل المنصف ( فإنه لأبلغ دليل على أن هذه القوة إنما هي من تدبير فاطر حكيم أوقفها عن الإنتاج في رأس هذا المستكبر ، جزاء لاستكباره ، وتحقيقاً لسبب عقابه الخالد يوم القيامة . فإذا تأملت في هذه البراهين التي عرضناها ، أدركت أن كلمة « الإلحاد » لا تعني شيئاً أكثر من مخاصمة العقل ، مهما كان نوع هذا الإلحاد ومنبعه ، ومهما كانت فلسفته أو دوافعه
And this is not the extent of their amazing delirium, but they go beyond that to denying that eyes are created in us for sight, ears for hearing, and the mind for thinking and understanding, for if they did not deny that, they would be obliged to say that they are created for final causes, and then they would be made for this benefit by a Maker who did that by will. So they flee from this entailment, even if it costs them to undertake burdens of obstinacy that the mind cannot conceive. So you see them saying: The eye met with sight by mere coincidence, and the ear met with hearing by mere coincidence as well, and this brain inside the skull met with thought by mere coincidence. (Also, I say: By my life and by the life of truth, this very delirium is among the most conclusive proofs of the existence of God! For the mind would not have failed to be guided to what is clearest before it, if its movement towards understanding things had been purely mechanical. But since it failed to understand despite its existence and the existence of all the components of understanding) after its possessor inclined to atheism regarding the essence of God and was too arrogant for fair reflection (then it is the most conclusive evidence that this power is from the arrangement of a wise Creator who stopped it from producing in the head of this arrogant one, as a recompense for his arrogance, and a realization of the cause of his eternal punishment on the Day of Resurrection. So if you reflect on these proofs that we have presented, you will realize that the word 'ilhad' (atheism) means nothing more than opposing the mind, whatever the type of this atheism and its source, and whatever its philosophy or motives.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage is a combined argument and definition. The author first describes the materialist position: they deny that eyes, ears, and the mind are created for their obvious purposes, claiming instead that these are mere coincidences. The author notes that this denial is an attempt to avoid the necessary conclusion that these organs are created for a purpose by a willing Maker. Then the author presents a striking argument: this very denial and irrationality itself become a proof for God's existence. If the mind, under normal conditions, would easily see the purposefulness of creation, but in the atheist it fails due to obstinacy and arrogance, that failure itself shows that the mind's operation is controlled by a wise Creator who withholds understanding as a punishment. Finally, the author defines 'ilhad' (atheism) as essentially opposing the mind, regardless of its specific form or philosophy.

Key Terms

مخاصمة العقل (opposing the mind)
براهين (proofs)
فاطر (Creator)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument is based on the impossibility of coincidence.
Correction: The author does not argue that coincidence is impossible; rather, he argues that the atheist's irrational denial of purpose, despite the mind's capacity to see it, reveals divine intervention.

Checkpoint

B) Because the mind's failure to see the obvious, despite its capacity, shows a divine withholding of understanding as punishment.
C) Because coincidences cannot happen.
D) Because the materialists admit there is no purpose.

Key Takeaway
The irrational denial of purpose itself becomes a proof for God, showing that atheism is a rebellion against reason.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage says that the mind fails to see the obvious due to arrogance. Is there a truth about Allah that you have resisted because accepting it would demand a change in your life? What would it cost you to submit to that truth today?
?
Al-Buti defines atheism as opposing the mind. But what about the subtle ways you oppose reason in your own heart—ignoring the purpose of your abilities or dismissing signs of Allah because they are uncomfortable? Will you examine those areas today?
?
The atheist's irrational denial is used as a proof. How about your own denials? Are there parts of your life where you act as if there is no Creator overseeing you? Ask Allah to remove the arrogance that blinds you, and commit to seeing His signs clearly.

Empirical Evidence Refutes Materialism
Buti cites scientific failure and testimony of scientists to refute the materialist claim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Buti uses empirical evidence from science's failure to create life and scientists' own admissions to refute materialism.

Core Idea
Science's mastery over matter yet ignorance of life proves life is not merely material.

Buti now moves from logical critique to empirical evidence. He challenges materialists: if life is a product of matter, why can't science produce it? He then cites leading scientists who admit their ignorance. This passage grounds the refutation in observable reality.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the rhetorical questions and the tree analogy.
The passage includes a quote from Engels and a narrative about a 1959 conference.
2
Understand the tree analogy
Buti compares matter to a tree and life to its fruit. If you know the tree completely, you should know the fruit. Science knows matter but not life—this is absurd.
This analogy highlights the inconsistency in materialism.
3
Examine Engels' admission
Engels, a founder of materialism, admitted that natural science has not produced life from chemicals. This is a powerful testimony from within the materialist camp.
Buti uses this quote to show even materialists acknowledge their ignorance.
4
Reflect on the 1959 conference
Six leading scientists from East and West, including Oparin, met to understand the origin of life. They concluded nothing except increased certainty of their ignorance.
This shows that despite decades of research, science has no explanation for life's origin.

Then this philosophy is refuted after that by the reality of tangible experience. For if life is only a fruit of the fruits of inert matter, then why do they not understand the secret of life, and why do they not produce life by chemical interaction, and why do they not identify the material elements from whose composition life was formed? The horizons of science have extended until they encompassed the particles of matter, its secrets, and its atoms, and even science disclosed the particles of the atom itself and the latent energies within it. Commentary
This passage is an empirical refutation of materialism. Buti argues that if life is merely a product of matter, then materialist scientists should be able to produce life through chemical means or at least understand its essence. But science, despite mastering the minutiae of matter, fails to do so with life. He uses the analogy of a tree: if one knows the tree completely, one should know its fruit; yet science knows matter but not life. He then quotes Engels, a founder of materialism, who admitted that natural science has not produced life from chemicals. Then he mentions the 1959 New York conference of top biologists (including Oparin) who failed to understand the origin of life, concluding only that they did not know. This empirical evidence supports the logical critique from the previous lesson, showing that materialism cannot even account for observable reality.

Science's Failure to Understand Life Refutes Materialism
Buti refutes materialism using science's own limitations regarding life.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the scientific community's own admission of ignorance about the nature of life serves as a powerful refutation of materialist philosophy.

Core Idea
Science's confession of ignorance about life undermines materialism from within.

Materialist philosophy claims that all reality is matter and that science can eventually explain everything, including life. However, as Dr. Buti demonstrates, the very founders and leading figures of materialism have admitted that science cannot understand life or the soul. This lesson examines that admission and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the tree analogy
Buti uses an analogy of a scientist who can analyze a tree in detail but cannot understand its fruit. This illustrates the paradox of science understanding matter but failing to understand life, which is its product. Reflect on what this analogy implies about materialist claims.
The analogy sets up the central argument: if science cannot grasp life, then materialism's core claim is falsified.
2
Examine the scientific consensus
Read the citation from Engels, a co-founder of materialism, admitting that natural science cannot produce life or affirm its origin. Then consider the 1959 conference where top scientists, including the materialist Oparin, concluded that life remains a mystery. Notice who is making these admissions.
The irony is that these are the very people who promoted materialism.
3
Draw the conclusion
Buti concludes that materialism is based on ignorance and illusion, and that its own proponents have exposed its flaws. Ask yourself: If science cannot explain life, what does that say about a philosophy that denies anything beyond matter?
This connects to the Islamic concept of al-ruh (soul) being from the unseen.

٢٣ . وانظر كتاب انتي دوهرنع لإنجلز ترجمة الدكتور فؤاد أيوب ص ٩٠
Science has scrutinized the very particles of the atom and the latent energies within them. How then can we comprehend that the authority of science extends to this extent concerning matter, which is the origin and source, and then its authority shrinks completely and is utterly lost concerning life, which is the fruit and branch? Has any person believed that a scientist was able to conduct a detailed analysis of a tree from its lowest trunk to its highest leaf, but when he wanted to know about its fruits, they became obscure to him and he understood nothing about them? Perhaps you say: What makes you think that they have not researched life and have not understood anything about it? The answer is that the consensus of all the world's scientists has agreed that science has not arrived at understanding anything about the reality of life, and that the subject of the soul (al-ruh) enters into the matters of the unseen (al-ghaybiyya) over which science has no authority. The first to acknowledge this ignorance was Engels, the colleague of Marx in formulating and promoting materialist philosophy. He says in his book 'Anti-Dühring': ('... It [meaning natural science] has not yet succeeded in producing simple matter and other unicellular bodies from chemical elements, and therefore it is not within the capacity of natural science, until the present time, to affirm anything concerning the origin of life.') Then time passed, and the sciences advanced, and the year 1959 came when six leading scientists of the East and West, specialists, met in New York City at a round table, to cooperate in understanding something about the origin and development of life on the surface of this earth. Among them was the Russian scientist Alexander Ivanovich Oparin, professor of biochemistry at the Academy of Sciences of the Soviet Union, and the most significant of those concerned with the issue of the origin of life. The conference ended as it began, with the participants only arriving at increased certainty that the matter of life is still unknown, and there is no hope that science will ever reach it. The first to affirm this was that Russian scientist himself. The summary of the statement - as Dr. Anwar Abd al-Alim says - is that science has not yet attained the discovery of this greatest secret known as life, and it becomes clear that this problem is far from being merely the construction of certain organic substances and specific natural and chemical phenomena. (1) And the great divine wisdom requires that this fact becomes increasingly confirmed and clear on the tongue of the Russian scientist himself. For in the aforementioned year 1959, news agencies, foremost among them the Soviet news agency TASS, circulated the following: Alexander Oparin, head of the Institute of Biochemistry in Russia, after having researched for 37 years on the origin of life and on researching whether it is possible to create the first cell through chemical reaction, announced that life cannot begin from nothing nor be generated from chemical reaction and spontaneous generation, and that science cannot delve beyond the limits of matter. So what meaning remains after this speech and what came before it for the materialist philosophy that Marx imagined one day out of a particular emotional impulse? ... And behold, you see that it is not we who remove from it its illusory philosophical veil behind which hides a great amount of ignorance and illusion, but rather the one who does that is the people of the house themselves, for a witness from among them has testified. And Allah sufficed the believers from fighting. As for the details of this philosophy and the examination of its propositions and laws, we are not now in [a position to discuss them] (1) See the report of this conference in the book 'The Story of Evolution' by Dr. Anwar Abd al-Alim, pp. 11-23. And see the book 'Anti-Dühring' by Engels, translation by Dr. Fu'ad Ayyub, p. 90.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of materialist philosophy, using the limitations of science as evidence. The author begins with an analogy: science can analyse a tree in detail but cannot understand its fruit; similarly, science can understand matter but not life. He then asks how we know that scientists have not understood life, and answers that there is a consensus among scientists that life and the soul (al-ruh) are beyond scientific investigation. He cites Engels, a co-founder of materialism, who admitted in 'Anti-Dühring' that natural science has not produced simple life from chemicals and cannot affirm anything about the origin of life. The author then describes a 1959 conference of top scientists, including the Russian materialist Oparin, who after 37 years of research concluded that life cannot arise from chemical reactions and that science cannot go beyond matter. The author highlights the irony that these admissions come from the very proponents of materialism, effectively refuting their own philosophy. He concludes that materialist philosophy is based on ignorance and illusion, and that its own adherents have exposed its flaws. The passage ends by noting that the details of materialism are not the current subject, but the core argument is that science's acknowledged ignorance about life and soul undermines the materialist claim that all reality is material.

Thought: Independent Gift from Allah, Not Product of Economics
Buti refutes materialism and argues thought is from Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Buti argues that thought cannot be a product of economic factors and must be an independent gift from Allah.

Core Idea
Economic need alone cannot produce thought; animals have the same needs but no thought.

Buti challenges the materialist claim that economic factors give rise to thought. He points to animals, who share the same economic needs but lack thought and civilization. This leads him to conclude that thought is an independent reality that comes from Allah, not from matter.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the structure of questions and answers.
2
Identify the materialist answer
Buti presents the materialist claim: economic need (means of production) ignites thought. Find that part and understand it.
The materialist answer is simple: need for food/drink sets thought in motion.
3
Understand the animal objection
Buti asks: why didn't animals, with the same needs, develop thought? This objection refutes materialism. Then see his conclusion: thought is from Allah.
This is the key refutation – think about why it works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والخلاصة ، أننا نطرح هذا السؤال : ما هو علة التطور الاجتماعي ؟ والجواب الواضح على لسان كل باحث : إنه الفكر . ولا بد أن نسأل : عامل انبعاث الفكر ؟ وتجيب المادية التاريخية على هذا السؤال الثاني بكل بساطة : إنه العامل الاقتصادي المتمثل في وسائل الإنتاج ، فالشعور بالحاجة إلى الطعام والشراب هو الذي حرك البذور الأولى للفكر والعقل ، وهو الذي فجّر أيضاً طاقة اللسان وقدرة التعبير . ولا بد أن يسأل كل عاقل في الدنيا : فلماذا تخلفت البهائم والسباع المختلفة ، عن زميلها « الإنسان » في هذه المرحلة التي تكافأت فيها الفرص، وأظلها نظام قانون واحد ؟ ولماذا استطاعت سياط الدياليكتيك أن تدفع بالإنسان إلى حيث وصل الآن ، دون أن تستطيع هذه السياط نفسها تحريك سائر الحيوانات الأخرى شبراً واحداً إلى الأمام ؟ فلا هي تمتعت بفكر ولا اغتنت بلغة ولا ازدهر فيها اقتصاد ! إن الجواب الذي لا مفر منه بحال من الأحوال ، هو أن الفكر حقيقة مستقلة تنزلت إلى الإنسان من لدن خالق الإنسان. وعبث لا طائل فيه أن تبحث للفكر عن جذور أو عوامل في دنيا المادة أو الاقتصاد أو وسيلة الإنتاج.
The conclusion is that we pose this question: What is the cause of social development? The clear answer from every researcher is: It is thought. We must ask: What is the factor that ignites thought? Historical materialism answers this second question very simply: It is the economic factor represented in the means of production, for the feeling of need for food and drink is what moved the first seeds of thought and intellect, and it is what also exploded the power of speech and the ability to express. Every rational person in the world must ask: Why did the various beasts and predators fall behind their companion 'man' in this stage when opportunities were equal and they were shaded by one legal system? And why were the whips of dialectics able to drive man to where he has now reached, while these same whips were unable to move all other animals even a single inch forward? So they did not enjoy thought, nor did they become rich with language, nor did economy flourish in them! The answer that is unavoidable under any circumstances is that thought is an independent reality that descended to man from the Creator of man. And it is futile and useless to search for roots or factors for thought in the world of matter, economics, or the means of production.

Commentary
This passage is a cumulative argument for the independent reality of thought, moving from a question-answer format to a decisive objection. Buti first establishes that everyone agrees the cause of social development is thought. He then presents the materialist answer: economic need ignites thought. To refute this, he poses the 'animal objection': if economic need were the cause of thought, then animals, who share the same needs for food and drink, should have developed thought and reached human-level civilization. But they did not—they have no thought, language, or economy. Therefore, the economic factor cannot be the cause. The only answer left is that thought is an independent reality that comes from God, not from matter. Thus, searching for material or economic roots for thought is futile.

Buti shows logical necessity from revelation to belief in God and Quranic content.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how accepting revelation logically necessitates belief in God and acceptance of all Quranic teachings.

Core Idea
Revelation verified → God exists → Quran's commands are binding.

Buti presents a clean logical chain: once we confirm that the Quran is true revelation, we cannot stop there. It forces us to believe in God, because the Quran speaks of Him and is backed by miracles. And then it forces us to accept everything the Quran says, including its commands and prohibitions. This lesson traces that two-step necessity.

The Skeptic's Confusion as a Proof for God
Buti argues that the skeptic's persistent doubt proves God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Buti turns the skeptic's persistent doubt into a powerful argument for God's existence.

Core Idea
The skeptic's confusion is itself a sign of God.

Buti presents a striking twist: the very fact that a rational person remains unconvinced after hearing all the proofs is itself evidence for God. If the intellect were left to itself, it would naturally reach the truth. Its failure to do so points to an external force—a Creator who can suspend its operation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation. Let Buti's argument unfold naturally.
The passage is cut off at the end but the argument is complete.
2
Understand Buti's premise
Notice that Buti assumes the intellect, if left alone, will naturally discover truth from premises. This is the key premise of the argument.
The intellect's natural function is to reach conclusions.
3
Identify the conclusion
Buti concludes that if the intellect fails to reach truth despite clear proofs, something must be stopping it. Only a great Creator with absolute authority could do that.
The skeptic's confusion becomes evidence for God.
4
Reflect on the argument's novelty
Think about how this argument differs from standard proofs. It uses doubt itself as a sign, not despite it.
This turns a common objection into a proof.

Commentary
This passage presents a novel argument: the very fact that a rational person remains unconvinced despite clear proofs is itself evidence for God's existence. Only a supreme being could have the absolute authority to suspend the intellect's natural function. Thus, the skeptic's persistent doubt points to the existence of God as the only force capable of arresting reason.

The Second Way: Quranic Testimony and Logical Certainty
Describes the second way to belief in God via the Quran and its miracles, and the logical compulsion of certainty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second way to belief in God as presented in the Quran, its logical compulsion, and how it leads to certainty that is reinforced by rational proofs.

Core Idea
The Quran's own testimony and miracles compel certainty in God and all it conveys.

This lesson introduces the second way to belief in God, which is based on the Quran itself and its miracles. Unlike the first way which relied on rational proofs, this way begins with the Quran's own testimony and the miracles supporting it, and shows that once certainty in God is attained, belief in all that the Quran conveys follows necessarily. The author emphasizes the logical compulsion: certain premises lead to a certain conclusion, and any doubt would be contradictory.

Guided Path
1
Identify components of the second way
Read the passage and note how the second way is defined: through the Quran and its miracles. What are the key elements?
The passage mentions the Quran itself, miracles, and the necessity of believing all its contents.
2
Understand the logical argument
Focus on the part where the author explains why certainty in premises compels certainty in conclusion. Why is doubt impossible?
The author compares doubt to accepting a contradiction: if premises are certain, doubt in conclusion would be like two opposites coexisting.
3
See how the two ways complement each other
Note how the second way leads to certainty, and then the first way's rational proofs add extra certainty, creating a scientific method immune to doubt.
The conclusion says both ways together provide a complete method.

Commentary
This passage describes the second way to belief in God's existence, which is based on the testimony of the Qur'an itself and the miracles supporting it, especially the Qur'an. The author argues that once one believes in God through this way, one must also believe in all that the Qur'an conveys – its news, commands, and prohibitions. He then explains the logical compulsion of this second way: the researcher, by progressing through the steps outlined, is necessarily led to belief in God, even without considering the rational proofs of the first way. This is because certainty in the premises necessitates certainty in the conclusion; to doubt the conclusion while firmly believing the premises would be contradictory, akin to affirming the co-existence of two opposites. Furthermore, the author notes that when the researcher attains this definitive conclusion, the rational proofs from the first way also become evident, reinforcing certainty and providing a comprehensive scientific method immune to doubt. The passage thus presents the second way as both self-sufficient and complementary to rational proofs.

Learning Objective

Core Idea
Irrational rejection of clear truth is itself a sign of God's control.

This lesson explores a unique argument: the very fact that some rational people reject overwhelming evidence for God's existence becomes evidence itself. It shows that intellect is not autonomous but subject to divine will, and that this phenomenon is a manifestation of Allah's established way.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully

Understand the logical core

4

وأخيراً ، فإذا رأيت إنساناً عاقلاً عرضت أمامه هذه البراهين كلها وبقي مع ذلك متململاً في شأنها ، شاكاً في نتيجتها ، لا يملك عليها أي ردّ ، ولكن لا يهتدي ورائها أيضاً إلى أي حق ، وهو مع ذلك حاضر الفكر والعقل ، فاعلم أنك من هذا الإنسان أمام دليل آخر على وجود الله عز وجل
ذلك لأن العقل إذا ترك وشأنه ، فلابد أن يعمل عمله الطبيعي في اكتشاف الحقائق والوصول عن طريق المقدمات إلى النتائج ، ولو لم يكن هناك موجد عظيم لهذا العقل ، له السلطان المطلق على عمله وسيره يستطيع أن يوقفه عن عمله عندما يشاء ويستطيع أن يصده عن فهم أبسط الحقائق في كل لحظة الزمن - لما توقف عقل هذا الإنسان عن فهم هذه الحقيقة البدهية الواضحة خصوصاً بعد النظر في براهينها اليقينية القاطعة
أما وقد وقع منه هذا العجز الغريب ، فإنه مصداق لسنة الله الجارية في عباده : ينير الطريق أمام العقل الذي لم يستكبر صاحبه عن التأمل في معرفة الحق منذ أول الطريق ، ولم يفضل اتباع شهواته على اتباع نداء عقله منذ أولى مراحل الفكر .. ويسد الطريق أمام العقل الذي استكبر منذ الخطوة الأولى ، إذ أعلن بلسان حاله أو مقاله أنه ليس على استعداد لأن يتبع الحق الذي يصده عن شهواته ويضيق عليه السبيل إلى أهوائه . فتراه بعد ذلك يفهم كل دقيق من شؤون الحياة المختلفة ، حتى إذا وضعته أمام أجلى حقيقة فيها وهي وجود الله عز وجل ، وجدته فيها كمجنون يتخبطه الشيطان من المس !..
وانظر كم هو واضح هذا المعنى في قول الله تعالى : ﴿ وَمَنْ أَظْلَمُ مِمَّنْ ذُكِّرَ بآياتِ رَبِّه فأعْرَضَ عَنْها وَنَسِيَ ما قَدَّمَتْ يَداهُ . إنا جَعَلْنَا عَلَى قُلُوبِهِمْ أَكِنّةً أَنْ يَفْقَهُوهُ وفي آذانِهِمْ وَقْراً وَإِنْ تَدْعُهُمْ إلى الهُدَى فَلَنْ يَهْتَدُوا إذا أبداً . ١ الكهف : ٥٧ ] .
•
أجل يا أخي القارئ !.. إن هذه الظاهرة لمن أجلى البراهين على وجود الله
Finally, if you see a rational person before whom all these proofs are presented, yet he remains restless concerning them, doubting their conclusion, having no rebuttal against them, but also not reaching any truth through them, while being of sound mind and intellect, then know that in this person you are facing another proof for the existence of God Almighty. That is because if the intellect is left to itself, it must perform its natural work of discovering truths and reaching conclusions via premises. If there were no great Creator of this intellect, having absolute authority over its operation and course, able to stop it from its work whenever He wills and able to prevent it from understanding the simplest truths at any moment of time, then this person's intellect would not have stopped from understanding this clear, obvious truth, especially after considering its definitive, certain proofs. Now that this strange inability has occurred from him, it is a manifestation of Allah's established way with His servants: He illuminates the path for the intellect whose owner did not become arrogant about contemplating knowledge of the truth from the beginning of the path, and did not prefer following his desires over following the call of his intellect from the earliest stages of thought; and He blocks the path for the intellect whose owner was arrogant from the first step, since he declared by his state or his words that he is not ready to follow the truth that would prevent him from his desires and constrict his path to his whims. So you see him thereafter understanding every subtlety of the various affairs of life, until you place before him the clearest truth among them – the existence of God Almighty – and you find him in it like a madman whom Satan has touched with insanity! And see how clear this meaning is in the saying of God Almighty: 'And who is more unjust than one who is reminded of the verses of his Lord, then turns away from them and forgets what his hands have put forth? Indeed, We have placed coverings over their hearts, lest they understand it, and in their ears is deafness. And if you invite them to guidance, they will never be guided, then ever.' [Al-Kahf: 57] Yes, my brother reader! Indeed, this phenomenon is among the clearest proofs of the existence of God.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage presents a final, subtle proof for God's existence: the phenomenon of willful rejection of clear evidence by a rational person. The author argues that when a person of sound mind is presented with all the proofs for God's existence and yet remains in doubt, unable to refute them but also unable to accept them, this very irrationality becomes evidence for God. The natural function of the intellect, when left to itself, is to reach conclusions from premises. If there were no Creator with absolute control over the intellect, such a person would necessarily have understood the self-evident truth of God's existence. The fact that he fails to do so indicates divine intervention – a manifestation of Allah's sunnah: He guides those who are humble and seek truth, but seals the hearts of the arrogant who prioritize desires over reason. This is supported by the Qur'anic verse (18:57) which speaks of those who turn away from God's signs and are prevented from understanding. The author concludes that this phenomenon itself is one of the clearest proofs of God's existence, as it shows that the intellect is not autonomous but subject to divine will.

العقل الطبيعي

استكبار

وقر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that rejection of proofs is due to lack of evidence or intellectual deficiency.
Correction: The author argues that rejection is due to arrogance and divine sealing, which itself proves God's existence and control over intellect.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the irrational rejection of clear proofs by a rational person demonstrate?
A) The proofs are insufficient.
B) The person lacks intelligence.
C) It is a proof of God's existence.
D) It is a purely psychological phenomenon.

Key Takeaway
The irrational rejection of clear proofs by a rational person is itself a sign of God's existence, demonstrating His control over the intellect.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When have you witnessed yourself resisting a clear truth because it would require you to change your desires? What excuse did your mind manufacture at that moment, and how does this passage expose that excuse as a sign of divine sealing rather than honest doubt?
?
The passage says that Allah 'blocks the path for the intellect whose owner was arrogant from the first step.' Reflect: in what area of your life—beliefs, habits, relationships—are you still not ready to follow the truth because it would constrict your whims? What concrete step would you take today to become a person of humility from the first step?
?
If someone's irrational rejection of God is itself a proof of God's existence, then your own moments of doubt or hardness of heart become evidence against your own soul. How does sitting with that uncomfortable truth change the way you pray for guidance tomorrow?

Allah's Existence
beginner
4 min
Denial as a Proof of God's Existence
Buti concludes that the inability to accept God is a clear proof of Him.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the phenomenon of denial itself serves as a proof for God's existence, according to Ramadan al-Buti.

Core Idea
The inability to accept God is itself a proof of His existence.

This lesson explores a unique argument for God's existence based on the psychology of denial. Ramadan al-Buti observes that some intelligent people, despite clear proofs, cannot accept God. He argues that this inability is not from lack of evidence but from spiritual arrogance, which itself points to a divine cause.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to understand the author's claim that denial is a proof.
Pay attention to the contrast between those who seek truth and those who turn away.
2
Identify the two types of people
Notice how Buti describes two paths: one for the humble seeker and one for the arrogant person who prefers desires.
This distinction is key to understanding the argument.
3
Connect to the Quranic verse
Read the verse from Surah Al-Kahf and see how it supports the idea that God seals hearts of those who turn away.
The verse is used as evidence for the sunnah.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Consider why the phenomenon of denial is considered one of the clearest proofs of God's existence.
Think about the cause-and-effect relationship between arrogance and spiritual blindness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من عمله عندما يشاء ويستطيع أن يصده عن فهم أبسط الحقائق في كل لحظة الزمن - لما توقف عقل هذا الإنسان عن فهم هذه الحقيقة البدهية الواضحة خصوصاً بعد النظر في براهينها اليقينية القاطعة. أما وقد وقع منه هذا العجز الغريب ، فإنه مصداق لسنة الله الجارية في عباده : ينير الطريق أمام العقل الذي لم يستكبر صاحبه عن التأمل في معرفة الحق منذ أول الطريق ، ولم يفضل اتباع شهواته على اتباع نداء عقلـه منـذ أولى مراحل الفكر .. ويسد الطريق أمام العقل الذي استكبر منذ الخطوة الأولى ، إذ أعلن بلسان حاله أو مقاله أنه ليس على استعداد لأن يتبع الحق الذي يصده عن شهواته ويضيق عليه السبيل إلى أهوائه . فتراه بعد ذلك يفهم كل دقيق من شؤون الحياة المختلفة ، حتى إذا وضعته أمام أجلى حقيقة فيها وهي وجود الله عز وجل ، وجدته فيها كمجنون يتخبطه الشيطان من المس !.. وانظر كم هو واضح هذا المعنى في قول الله تعالى : ﴿ وَمَنْ أَظْلَمُ مِمَّنْ ذُكِّرَ بآياتِ رَبِّه فأعْرَضَ عَنْها وَنَسِيَ ما قَدَّمَتْ يَداهُ . إنا جَعَلْنَا عَلَى قُلُوبِهِمْ أَكِنّةً أَنْ يَفْقَهُوهُ وفي آذانِهِمْ وَقْراً وَإِنْ تَدْعُهُمْ إلى الهُدَى فَلَنْ يَهْتَدُوا إذا أبداً . 1 الكهف : ٥٧ ] . أجل يا أخي القارئ !.. إن هذه الظاهرة لمن أجلى البراهين على وجود الله
From His action when He wills and is able to prevent him from understanding the simplest truths at every moment of time - when the mind of this person stops understanding this obvious clear truth, especially after considering its decisive certain proofs. And since this strange inability has occurred from him, it is an embodiment of Allah's ongoing sunnah among His servants: He illuminates the path for the mind whose owner did not become arrogant about reflecting upon knowing the truth from the beginning of the path, and did not prefer following his desires over following the call of his mind from the first stages of thought. And He blocks the path for the mind whose owner became arrogant from the first step, for he declared by his state or his words that he is not prepared to follow the truth that prevents him from his desires and narrows the way to his whims. So you see him after that understanding every subtle matter of various worldly affairs, until when you place him before the clearest truth among them, which is the existence of Allah Almighty, you find him in it like a madman possessed by Satan from touch! And see how clear this meaning is in the saying of Allah Almighty: 'And who is more unjust than one who is reminded of the verses of his Lord and then turns away from them and forgets what his hands have put forth? Indeed, We have placed over their hearts coverings, lest they understand it, and in their ears deafness. And if you invite them to guidance, they will never be guided, ever.' [Surah Al-Kahf 18:57]. Yes, my dear reader! Indeed, this phenomenon is among the clearest proofs of the existence of Allah.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage concludes a proof for God's existence by reflecting on a psychological phenomenon. The author argues that a person who can grasp complex worldly matters yet becomes utterly confused when faced with the obvious truth of God's existence – especially after clear proofs have been presented – is an example of God's sunnah (divine practice). The sunnah is that God guides those who are humble and seek truth from the beginning, but He seals the hearts of those who are arrogant and prefer their desires. The author then quotes Quran 18:57 to illustrate this: those who turn away from God's signs are rendered unable to understand. The passage ends by stating that this very phenomenon is among the clearest proofs of God's existence, because it shows that the denial is not due to lack of evidence but due to a spiritual condition, which itself points to a divine cause.

Key Terms
سنة الله
براهين
عقل
شهوات
آيات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the inability to accept God's existence is due to lack of intelligence or evidence.
Correction: The author clarifies it is due to arrogance and sin, which is itself a proof of God.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the reason a person fails to understand the clear truth of God's existence despite having intellect?
A) Lack of intelligence or education
B) Arrogance and preference for desires from the beginning
C) Inadequate proofs
D) The complexity of the concept

Key Takeaway
The phenomenon of denial, rooted in arrogance, is itself a proof of God's existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter someone who vigorously denies God despite clear arguments, does your reaction align with the author's conclusion that their denial is itself a proof of God? Or do you become frustrated, questioning why they cannot see? What does your reaction reveal about your own trust in divine wisdom and justice? Commit to seeing such denial as a sign of Allah's power and sunnah, not as a failure of evidence.
?
The author says the arrogant person 'declared by his state or his words that he is not prepared to follow the truth that prevents him from his desires and narrows the way to his whims.' In what specific area of your own life have you done the same—resisting a truth that would curb a cherished desire? Take a moment today to identify one such truth you have been avoiding and sincerely ask Allah to soften your heart to it.
?
If Allah 'blocks the path' for the arrogant, could it be that some of your own struggles to understand or accept certain Islamic teachings are rooted in arrogance rather than sincere inquiry? Reflect on a time when you felt confused or resistant toward a clear command of Allah. Was there an element of pride or attachment to your own opinion? Repent and ask Allah to guide you like the humble seeker described in the passage.
